<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Natural gas</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="863" data-file-width="1190" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png/330px-Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png/495px-Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png/660px-Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Global_Gas_trade_both_LNG_and_Pipeline.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The global <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_exports" title="List of countries by natural gas exports">natural gas trade</a> in 2013. Numbers are in billion cubic meters per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png/330px-World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png/495px-World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png/660px-World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_-_Natural_Gas_Production_of_Countries.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_production" title="List of countries by natural gas production">Natural gas extraction by countries</a> in cubic meters per year around 2013.</div></div></div>
<p><b>Natural gas</b> is a naturally occurring <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a> <a href="/wiki/Gas" title="Gas">gas</a> mixture consisting primarily of <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a>, but commonly including varying amounts of other higher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alkanes" title="Alkanes">alkanes</a>, and sometimes a small percentage of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">hydrogen sulfide</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Helium" title="Helium">helium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> It is formed when layers of decomposing plant and animal matter are exposed to intense heat and pressure under the surface of the Earth over millions of years. The energy that the plants originally obtained from the sun is stored in the form of chemical bonds in the gas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epa_ng_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-epa_ng-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Natural gas is a <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuel</a> used as a source of energy for heating, cooking, and electricity generation. It is also used as a <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_vehicle" title="Natural gas vehicle">fuel for vehicles</a> and as a chemical feedstock in the manufacture of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plastics" title="Plastics">plastics</a> and other commercially important <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organic chemicals</a>. Fossil fuel based natural gas is a <a href="/wiki/Non-renewable_resource" title="Non-renewable resource">non-renewable resource</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epa_ng_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-epa_ng-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>Natural gas is found in deep underground rock formations or associated with other hydrocarbon reservoirs in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coal_bed" title="Coal bed">coal beds</a> and as <a href="/wiki/Methane_clathrate" title="Methane clathrate">methane clathrates</a>. <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Petroleum</a> is another resource and fossil fuel found in close proximity to and with natural gas. Most natural gas was created over time by two mechanisms: biogenic and thermogenic. Biogenic gas is created by <a href="/wiki/Methanogen" title="Methanogen">methanogenic</a> organisms in <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">marshes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bog" title="Bog">bogs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfills</a>, and shallow sediments. Deeper in the earth, at greater temperature and pressure, thermogenic gas is created from buried organic material.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>In petroleum production gas is often burnt as <a href="/wiki/Gas_flare" title="Gas flare">flare gas</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> estimates that over 150 cubic kilometers of natural gas are flared or vented annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Before natural gas can be used as a fuel, most, but not all, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_gas_processing" title="Natural gas processing">must be processed</a> to remove impurities, including water, to meet the specifications of marketable natural gas. The by-products of this processing include: <a href="/wiki/Ethane" title="Ethane">ethane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Propane" title="Propane">propane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butane" title="Butane">butanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentane" title="Pentane">pentanes</a>, and higher molecular weight hydrocarbons, hydrogen sulfide (which may be converted into pure <a href="/wiki/Sulfur" title="Sulfur">sulfur</a>), <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_vapor" title="Water vapor">water vapor</a>, and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Helium" title="Helium">helium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a>.
</p><p>Natural gas is often informally referred to simply as "gas", especially when compared to other energy sources such as oil or coal. However, it is not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Gasoline" title="Gasoline">gasoline</a>, especially in North America, where the term gasoline is often shortened in colloquial usage to <i>gas</i>.
</p>
